Minor's Agency and Litigation
Ruling on minor's capacity in agency and litigation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a minor's agency and litigation are valid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A minor's agency and litigation are valid only if he is authorized and capable of understanding the contract.

This opening passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, quoting al-Multaqat, establishes the baseline for a minor's legal capacity in financial dealings. It distinguishes between the minor acting for himself versus acting for others. The key principle is that the minor's statements (like contracts) are not binding on him but can be binding on his principal if he is properly authorized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act: agency or litigation
Determine whether the minor is acting as an agent (وكيل) or as a litigant (خصم). The ruling differs.
Agency is about contracting for another; litigation is about legal proceedings.
2
Check authorization status
Is the minor authorized (مأذون) by his guardian? If not, he is under interdiction (محجور) and his actions are restricted.
The text explicitly states that litigation is only valid if the minor is authorized (مأذون).
3
Understand the effect of his action
If the minor acts as an agent, the rights and obligations revert to the principal, not to the minor. For example, in a sale, the buyer deals with the principal.
The text says: 'لا ترجع الحقوق إليه في نحو بيع بل لموكله'.
4
Apply the rule for zakat and gifts
In giving zakat, the intention (نية) is that of the principal, not the minor agent. The minor's word is accepted in transactions like gifts, meaning his statement that he gave or received a gift is taken as true.
This is an exception: 'ويعمل بقول المميز في المعاملات كهدية ونحوها'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الملتقط
ويصح توكيله إذا كان يعقد العقد ويقصده ولو محجورا، ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه في نحو بيع بل لموكله وكذا في دفع الزكاة والاعتبار لنيَّة الموكل، ويعمل بقول المميز في المعاملات كهدية ونحوها وفي الملتقط ولا تصح الخصومة من الصبي إلا أن يكون مأذونا . (اهـ).
·
ويحصل بوطئه التحليل للمطلقة ثلاثا إذا كان مراهقا تتحرك آلته النساء . ويشتهي ويملك المال بالاستيلاء على المُباح كالبالغ، والتقاطه كالتقاط البالغ، ويجب ردّ سلامه، ويصح إسلامه وردته ولا يقتل لو ارتد بعد إسلامه صغيرًا أو تبعًا. وتحلّ ذبيحته بشرط أن يعقل التسمية ويضبطها بأن يعلم أن الحل لا يحصل إلا بها؛ كذا في الكافي. ويؤكل الصيد برميه إذا سمى، وليس كالبالغ في النظر إلى الأجنبية والخلوة بها فيجوز له الدخول على النساء إلى خمس عشرة سنة، كما في الملتقط. ولا يقع طلاقه ولا عتقه إلا حكمًا في مسائل ذكرناها في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الطلاق، والحجر عليه في الأقوال كلها لا في الأفعال فيضمن ما أتلفه إلا في مسائل ذكرناه في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الحجر، وتثبت حرمة المصاهرة بوطئه إن كان ممن يشتهي النساء وإلا فلا. وتثبت أيضًا بوطء الصبية المشتهاة وهي بنت تسع على المختار، ولا يدخل الصبي في القسامة ،والعاقلة وإن وجد قتيل في داره فالدية على عاقلته كما في الصغرى، ولا جزية عليه ولا يدخل في الغرامات السلطانية كما في قسمة الولوالجية، ولا يؤخذ صبيان أهل الذمة بالتمييز عن صبيان المسلمين كما في الخانية، ولا شيء على صبيان بني تغلب.
ولا يقتل ولد الحربي إذا لم يقاتل، ولو قتله مجاهد بعد قول الإمام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه لم يستحق السلب إلا إذا قاتل، ويدخل الصبي تحت قوله من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه فإذا قتل الصبي استحق سلب مقتوله لقول الزيلعي: ويدخل فيه كل من يستحق الغنيمة سهما أو رضحًا. (انتهى).
،
وفي الكنز أن الصبي ممن يرضخ له إذا قاتل ولو قال السلطان لصبي إذا أدركت فصل بالناس الجمعة جاز، وفي البزازية السلطان أو الوالي إذا كان غير بالغ
فبلغ يحتاج إلى تقليد جديد. (انتهى).
ولا تنعقد يمينه ولو كان مأذونا فباع فوجد المشتري به عيبا لا يحلفه حتى يدرك كما في العمدة، ولو ادَّعى على صبي محجور ولا بينة له لا يحضره إلى باب القاضي لأنه لو حلف فنكل لا يقضي عليه كذا في العمدة ويُقام التعزير عليه تأديبا، وتتوقف عقوده المترددة بين النفع والضرر على إجازة وليه ويصح قبضه للهبة، ولا
يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا ومنه إقراضه واستقراضه لو كان محجورًا، لا لو كان مأذونا وكفالته باطلة ولو عن أبيه، وصحت له وعنه مطلقا .
وقد جمع العمادي في فصوله أحكام الصبيان فمن أراد الاطلاع على كثرة فروعنا وحُسْن تقريرنا واستيعابنا وعلى نِعَم الله تعالى علينا فيما نقصده من جمع المتفرق فلينظر ما ذكره العمادي، وقد ذكر العمادي ما يكون به بالغا، وما يتعلق به تركناه قصدًا لتصريحهم به في كتاب الحجر، وكتابنا هذا إن شاء الله تعالى كتاب المفردات الملتقطات .
الصبية التي لا تُشتَهَى يجوز السفر بها بغير محرم ولا يضمن الصبي بالغصب فلو غصب صبيا فمات عنده لم يضمنه إلا إذا نقله إلى أرض مسبعة أو مكان الوباء أو الحمى، وقد سُئِلتُ عمَّن أخذ ابن إنسان صغيرًا وأخرجه من البلد هل يلزمه إحضاره إلى أبيه ؟ فأجبت بما في الخانية :
رجل غصب صبيا حرًا فغاب الصبي عن يده فإن الغاصب يُحبَس حتى يجيء بالصبي أو يعلم أنه مات (انتهى). ولو خدعه حتى أخذه برضاه لم يضمن كما في الخانية، لأنه ما غصبه لأنه الأخذ قهرًا وفي الملتقط من النكاح وعن محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيمن خدع بنت رجل أو امرأته وأخرجها من منزله. قال أحبسه أبدًا حتى يأتي بها أو يعلم موتها. (انتهى). ولو قطع طرف صبي لم تعلم صحته ففيه حكومة عدل لا دية ولو دفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل نفسه لم يضمن الدافع، وإن قتل غيره فالدية على عاقلة الصبي، ويرجعون بها على الدافع. وكذا لو أمر صبيا بقتل إنسان فقتله، ولو أمر صبيا بالوقوع من شجرة فوقع ضمن ديته، ولو أرسله في حاجة فعطب ضمنه وكذا لو أمره بصعود شجرة لنقض ثمارها فوقع، وكذا لو أمره بكسر الحطب كذا في الخانية، وفيها أيضًا : صبي ابن تسع سنين سقط من سطح أو غرق في ماء ؛ قال بعضهم لا شيء على الوالدين لأنه ممن يحفظ نفسه، وإن كان لا يعقل أو كان أصغر سنًا ؛ قالوا يكون على الوالدين أو على من كان الصبي في حجره الكفارة لترك الحفظ، وقال بعضهم ليس على الوالدين شيء إلا الاستغفار وهو الصحيح، إلا أن يسقط من يده فعليه الكفَّارة، ولو حمل صبيا على دابة وقال أمسكها لي وهي واقفة فسقط ومات كان على عاقلة الذي حمله الدية مطلقا، وإن سير الصبي الدابة فوطأت إنسانًا فقتلته فالدّية على عاقلة الصبي، إلا أن يكون الصبي
Al-Multaqat. His agency is valid if he contracts and intends it, even if under guardianship, and rights do not revert to him in transactions like sale, but to his principal; similarly in giving zakat, consideration is to the principal's intention, and the discerning minor's word is accepted in transactions like gifts and similar; in al-Multaqat: litigation from a minor is not valid unless he is authorized. (End). And his intercourse effects tahlil for a thrice-divorced woman if he is an adolescent whose organ is aroused by women and he desires. He owns property by seizing permissible things like an adult, and his finding (luqata) is like that of an adult, and his greeting must be returned. His Islam and apostasy are valid, but he is not killed if he apostatizes after becoming Muslim as a minor or by following. His slaughter is lawful provided he understands the tasmiya and grasps it, knowing that lawfulness is only attained by it; thus in al-Kafi. His game is eaten by his shot if he says the name, and he is not like an adult in looking at a non-mahram woman or seclusion with her; he may enter upon women up to fifteen years, as in al-Multaqat. His divorce and manumission do not take effect except legally in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in divorce; and he is under interdiction in all statements, not in actions, so he guarantees what he destroys, except in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in interdiction. The prohibition of affinity is established by his intercourse if he is one who desires women, otherwise not. It is also established by intercourse with a desired girl who is nine years old according to the chosen view. The minor does not enter into qasama, and the 'aqila: if a slain person is found in his house, the diya is on his 'aqila as in al-Sughra. No jizya on him, nor does he enter into government fines as in Qismat al-Walwalijiyya. The children of dhimmis are not distinguished from Muslim children as in al-Khaniyya, and nothing is on the children of Banu Taghlib. The child of a harbi is not killed if he does not fight, and if a fighter kills him after the imam's saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', he does not deserve the spoils unless he fought. The minor enters under the saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', so if a minor kills, he deserves the spoils of his victim due to al-Zayla'i's saying: everyone who deserves a share of booty or a small grant enters it. (End). And in al-Kanz: the minor is one who is given a small grant if he fights. If the sultan says to a minor 'when you reach puberty, lead the people in Friday prayer', it is permissible. In al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan or governor is not an adult and then reaches puberty, he needs a new appointment. (End). His oath is not valid, even if authorized; if he sells and the buyer finds a defect, he does not make him swear until he reaches puberty as in al-Umda. If a claim is made against a minor under guardianship and the claimant has no evidence, he is not brought to the judge's door because if he were to swear and then refuse, no judgment would be passed against him, thus in al-Umda. Ta'zir is established upon him as discipline. His contracts that are ambiguous between benefit and harm are contingent on his guardian's permission. His acceptance of a gift is valid. And among his statements that are purely harmful are not subject to [contingency], including his lending and borrowing if he is under guardianship, not if authorized. His suretyship is void even if for his father, but valid for him and from him absolutely. Al-Umadi has collected the rulings of minors in his chapters; whoever wishes to see the abundance of our branches, the goodness of our presentation, and our comprehensiveness, and the blessings of Allah upon us in our aim of gathering scattered [rulings], let him look at what al-Umadi mentioned. And al-Umadi has mentioned what makes one an adult, and what relates to that we have omitted intentionally because they have stated it in the book of interdiction, and this book of ours, Allah willing, is the book of unique collected items. A girl who is not desired: it is permissible to travel with her without a mahram. A minor does not guarantee by usurpation; if someone usurps a minor and he dies in his possession, he does not guarantee him unless he moved him to a land full of beasts or a place of plague or fever. I was asked about one who took a small son of a person and took him out of the town: is he required to bring him back to his father? I answered with what is in al-Khaniyya: A man usurped a free minor and the minor disappeared from his hand; then the usurper is imprisoned until he brings the minor or learns that he died. (End). If he tricked him until he took him with his consent, he does not guarantee, as in al-Khaniyya, because he did not usurp him since usurpation is taking by force. In al-Multaqat from Nikah: from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, concerning one who tricked a man's daughter or his wife and took her out of his house. He said: I would imprison him forever until he brings her or knows her death. (End). If someone cuts a limb of a minor whose health is unknown, there is an equitable assessment (hukumat 'adl), not diya. If someone hands a knife to a minor and he kills himself, the giver does not guarantee; if he kills another, the diya is on the minor's 'aqila, and they claim it back from the giver. Similarly, if he orders a minor to kill a man and he kills him. If he orders a minor to fall from a tree and he falls, he guarantees his diya. If he sends him on an errand and he perishes, he guarantees him; similarly, if he orders him to climb a tree to pick its fruits and he falls, and similarly if he orders him to break firewood, thus in al-Khaniyya. In it also: a minor of nine years fell from a roof or drowned in water; some say nothing is on the parents because he is one who can protect himself; if he was not intelligent or younger, they said there is kaffara on the parents or on the one in whose care the minor was for neglecting protection; and some said nothing is on the parents except seeking forgiveness, and that is the correct view, unless he fell from his hand, then kaffara is upon him. If he placed a minor on an animal and said 'hold it for me' while it was standing, and the minor fell and died, the diya is on the 'aqila of the one who placed him absolutely. If the minor made the animal walk and it trampled a man and killed him, the diya is on the minor's 'aqila, unless the minor...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal rulings regarding minors (الصبيان) drawn from various authoritative Hanafi sources such as al-Multaqat, al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, al-Umda, al-Kanz, al-Bazzaziyya, and others. The text covers a wide range of fiqh chapters, demonstrating that a minor's legal capacity is nuanced: in some areas (like owning property by seizure, accepting gifts, slaughter with conditions) the minor is treated similarly to an adult, while in others (like divorce, manumission, oaths, litigation) their actions are either invalid or contingent upon guardianship. Key principles include: (1) the discerning minor (المميز) has limited capacity in transactions; (2) the minor's intention (niyyah) is considered in matters like zakat where the principal's intention is paramount; (3) the minor's criminal liability is limited – their 'aqila pays diya for unintended killings, but they are not subject to qasama or jizya; (4) in worship, the minor's Islam and apostasy are valid, but apostasy does not incur execution; (5) the minor's testimony and oaths are not accepted; (6) contracts that are purely harmful are void, while those with potential benefit require guardian approval. The passage also notes the authority of al-Umadi's collection for further details. Overall, it reflects the Hanafi approach of balancing the minor's evolving capacity with protective guardianship.

Key Terms
الصبي (al-sabi): A male minor who has not reached puberty.
المحجور (al-mahjur): A minor under legal guardianship, whose financial actions require guardian approval.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A minor who has been granted permission to engage in trade, giving him limited capacity in transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a minor's litigation valid?
A) Always, if he is discerning.
B) Only if he is authorized (مأذون).
C) Only if he is above 15 years old.
D) It is never valid.

Key Takeaway
A minor's agency is valid if he understands the contract; litigation requires explicit authorization.

Minor in Worship and Family Law
Rulings on minor's capacity in worship and family law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on a minor's slaughter, apostasy, tahlil, and the establishment of affinity through intercourse.

Core Idea
A minor's religious acts are valid if conditions are met, but family law effects (divorce, manumission) are limited.

This section addresses the minor's involvement in worship (slaughter, hunting) and family matters (tahlil, marriage, divorce, manumission, affinity). The rulings vary based on the minor's physical maturity and understanding, reflecting the Hanafi balance between recognizing natural capacity and protecting the minor's interests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act as worship or family
Worship acts like slaughter and hunting require specific conditions; family acts like tahlil, marriage, and divorce have different criteria.
Slaughter involves tasmiya, tahlil involves sexual desire.
2
Check the minor's understanding and maturity
For slaughter, the minor must understand that lawfulness depends on tasmiya. For tahlil, the minor must be an adolescent (مراهق) with sexual desire. For divorce and manumission, they do not take effect except in specific cases.
The text mentions 'مراهقا تتحرك آلته النساء' for tahlil.
3
Apply the ruling specific to each case
Slaughter: lawful if he understands tasmiya. Hunting: his game is eaten if he says the name. Islam/apostasy: valid, but no execution for apostasy. Tahlil: effective if he is an adolescent. Affinity: established by his intercourse if he desires women; also by intercourse with a desired girl of nine. Divorce/manumission: not effective except in some cases.
These are exceptions to the general rule that minors' statements are invalid.
4
Note the age limit for entering upon women
The minor is allowed to enter upon women up to age fifteen, as he is not considered a threat like an adult male.
This is from al-Multaqat.

الملتقط
ويصح توكيله إذا كان يعقد العقد ويقصده ولو محجورا، ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه في نحو بيع بل لموكله وكذا في دفع الزكاة والاعتبار لنيَّة الموكل، ويعمل بقول المميز في المعاملات كهدية ونحوها وفي الملتقط ولا تصح الخصومة من الصبي إلا أن يكون مأذونا . (اهـ).
·
ويحصل بوطئه التحليل للمطلقة ثلاثا إذا كان مراهقا تتحرك آلته النساء . ويشتهي ويملك المال بالاستيلاء على المُباح كالبالغ، والتقاطه كالتقاط البالغ، ويجب ردّ سلامه، ويصح إسلامه وردته ولا يقتل لو ارتد بعد إسلامه صغيرًا أو تبعًا. وتحلّ ذبيحته بشرط أن يعقل التسمية ويضبطها بأن يعلم أن الحل لا يحصل إلا بها؛ كذا في الكافي. ويؤكل الصيد برميه إذا سمى، وليس كالبالغ في النظر إلى الأجنبية والخلوة بها فيجوز له الدخول على النساء إلى خمس عشرة سنة، كما في الملتقط. ولا يقع طلاقه ولا عتقه إلا حكمًا في مسائل ذكرناها في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الطلاق، والحجر عليه في الأقوال كلها لا في الأفعال فيضمن ما أتلفه إلا في مسائل ذكرناه في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الحجر، وتثبت حرمة المصاهرة بوطئه إن كان ممن يشتهي النساء وإلا فلا. وتثبت أيضًا بوطء الصبية المشتهاة وهي بنت تسع على المختار، ولا يدخل الصبي في القسامة ،والعاقلة وإن وجد قتيل في داره فالدية على عاقلته كما في الصغرى، ولا جزية عليه ولا يدخل في الغرامات السلطانية كما في قسمة الولوالجية، ولا يؤخذ صبيان أهل الذمة بالتمييز عن صبيان المسلمين كما في الخانية، ولا شيء على صبيان بني تغلب.
ولا يقتل ولد الحربي إذا لم يقاتل، ولو قتله مجاهد بعد قول الإمام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه لم يستحق السلب إلا إذا قاتل، ويدخل الصبي تحت قوله من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه فإذا قتل الصبي استحق سلب مقتوله لقول الزيلعي: ويدخل فيه كل من يستحق الغنيمة سهما أو رضحًا. (انتهى).
،
وفي الكنز أن الصبي ممن يرضخ له إذا قاتل ولو قال السلطان لصبي إذا أدركت فصل بالناس الجمعة جاز، وفي البزازية السلطان أو الوالي إذا كان غير بالغ
فبلغ يحتاج إلى تقليد جديد. (انتهى).
ولا تنعقد يمينه ولو كان مأذونا فباع فوجد المشتري به عيبا لا يحلفه حتى يدرك كما في العمدة، ولو ادَّعى على صبي محجور ولا بينة له لا يحضره إلى باب القاضي لأنه لو حلف فنكل لا يقضي عليه كذا في العمدة ويُقام التعزير عليه تأديبا، وتتوقف عقوده المترددة بين النفع والضرر على إجازة وليه ويصح قبضه للهبة، ولا
يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا ومنه إقراضه واستقراضه لو كان محجورًا، لا لو كان مأذونا وكفالته باطلة ولو عن أبيه، وصحت له وعنه مطلقا .
وقد جمع العمادي في فصوله أحكام الصبيان فمن أراد الاطلاع على كثرة فروعنا وحُسْن تقريرنا واستيعابنا وعلى نِعَم الله تعالى علينا فيما نقصده من جمع المتفرق فلينظر ما ذكره العمادي، وقد ذكر العمادي ما يكون به بالغا، وما يتعلق به تركناه قصدًا لتصريحهم به في كتاب الحجر، وكتابنا هذا إن شاء الله تعالى كتاب المفردات الملتقطات .
الصبية التي لا تُشتَهَى يجوز السفر بها بغير محرم ولا يضمن الصبي بالغصب فلو غصب صبيا فمات عنده لم يضمنه إلا إذا نقله إلى أرض مسبعة أو مكان الوباء أو الحمى، وقد سُئِلتُ عمَّن أخذ ابن إنسان صغيرًا وأخرجه من البلد هل يلزمه إحضاره إلى أبيه ؟ فأجبت بما في الخانية :
رجل غصب صبيا حرًا فغاب الصبي عن يده فإن الغاصب يُحبَس حتى يجيء بالصبي أو يعلم أنه مات (انتهى). ولو خدعه حتى أخذه برضاه لم يضمن كما في الخانية، لأنه ما غصبه لأنه الأخذ قهرًا وفي الملتقط من النكاح وعن محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيمن خدع بنت رجل أو امرأته وأخرجها من منزله. قال أحبسه أبدًا حتى يأتي بها أو يعلم موتها. (انتهى). ولو قطع طرف صبي لم تعلم صحته ففيه حكومة عدل لا دية ولو دفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل نفسه لم يضمن الدافع، وإن قتل غيره فالدية على عاقلة الصبي، ويرجعون بها على الدافع. وكذا لو أمر صبيا بقتل إنسان فقتله، ولو أمر صبيا بالوقوع من شجرة فوقع ضمن ديته، ولو أرسله في حاجة فعطب ضمنه وكذا لو أمره بصعود شجرة لنقض ثمارها فوقع، وكذا لو أمره بكسر الحطب كذا في الخانية، وفيها أيضًا : صبي ابن تسع سنين سقط من سطح أو غرق في ماء ؛ قال بعضهم لا شيء على الوالدين لأنه ممن يحفظ نفسه، وإن كان لا يعقل أو كان أصغر سنًا ؛ قالوا يكون على الوالدين أو على من كان الصبي في حجره الكفارة لترك الحفظ، وقال بعضهم ليس على الوالدين شيء إلا الاستغفار وهو الصحيح، إلا أن يسقط من يده فعليه الكفَّارة، ولو حمل صبيا على دابة وقال أمسكها لي وهي واقفة فسقط ومات كان على عاقلة الذي حمله الدية مطلقا، وإن سير الصبي الدابة فوطأت إنسانًا فقتلته فالدّية على عاقلة الصبي، إلا أن يكون الصبي
Al-Multaqat. His agency is valid if he contracts and intends it, even if under guardianship, and rights do not revert to him in transactions like sale, but to his principal; similarly in giving zakat, consideration is to the principal's intention, and the discerning minor's word is accepted in transactions like gifts and similar; in al-Multaqat: litigation from a minor is not valid unless he is authorized. (End). And his intercourse effects tahlil for a thrice-divorced woman if he is an adolescent whose organ is aroused by women and he desires. He owns property by seizing permissible things like an adult, and his finding (luqata) is like that of an adult, and his greeting must be returned. His Islam and apostasy are valid, but he is not killed if he apostatizes after becoming Muslim as a minor or by following. His slaughter is lawful provided he understands the tasmiya and grasps it, knowing that lawfulness is only attained by it; thus in al-Kafi. His game is eaten by his shot if he says the name, and he is not like an adult in looking at a non-mahram woman or seclusion with her; he may enter upon women up to fifteen years, as in al-Multaqat. His divorce and manumission do not take effect except legally in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in divorce; and he is under interdiction in all statements, not in actions, so he guarantees what he destroys, except in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in interdiction. The prohibition of affinity is established by his intercourse if he is one who desires women, otherwise not. It is also established by intercourse with a desired girl who is nine years old according to the chosen view. The minor does not enter into qasama, and the 'aqila: if a slain person is found in his house, the diya is on his 'aqila as in al-Sughra. No jizya on him, nor does he enter into government fines as in Qismat al-Walwalijiyya. The children of dhimmis are not distinguished from Muslim children as in al-Khaniyya, and nothing is on the children of Banu Taghlib. The child of a harbi is not killed if he does not fight, and if a fighter kills him after the imam's saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', he does not deserve the spoils unless he fought. The minor enters under the saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', so if a minor kills, he deserves the spoils of his victim due to al-Zayla'i's saying: everyone who deserves a share of booty or a small grant enters it. (End). And in al-Kanz: the minor is one who is given a small grant if he fights. If the sultan says to a minor 'when you reach puberty, lead the people in Friday prayer', it is permissible. In al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan or governor is not an adult and then reaches puberty, he needs a new appointment. (End). His oath is not valid, even if authorized; if he sells and the buyer finds a defect, he does not make him swear until he reaches puberty as in al-Umda. If a claim is made against a minor under guardianship and the claimant has no evidence, he is not brought to the judge's door because if he were to swear and then refuse, no judgment would be passed against him, thus in al-Umda. Ta'zir is established upon him as discipline. His contracts that are ambiguous between benefit and harm are contingent on his guardian's permission. His acceptance of a gift is valid. And among his statements that are purely harmful are not subject to [contingency], including his lending and borrowing if he is under guardianship, not if authorized. His suretyship is void even if for his father, but valid for him and from him absolutely. Al-Umadi has collected the rulings of minors in his chapters; whoever wishes to see the abundance of our branches, the goodness of our presentation, and our comprehensiveness, and the blessings of Allah upon us in our aim of gathering scattered [rulings], let him look at what al-Umadi mentioned. A girl who is not desired: it is permissible to travel with her without a mahram. A minor does not guarantee by usurpation; if someone usurps a minor and he dies in his possession, he does not guarantee him unless he moved him to a land full of beasts or a place of plague or fever. I was asked about one who took a small son of a person and took him out of the town: is he required to bring him back to his father? I answered with what is in al-Khaniyya: A man usurped a free minor and the minor disappeared from his hand; then the usurper is imprisoned until he brings the minor or learns that he died. (End). In al-Multaqat from Nikah: from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, concerning one who tricked a man's daughter or his wife and took her out of his house. He said: I would imprison him forever until he brings her or knows her death. (End). If someone cuts a limb of a minor whose health is unknown, there is an equitable assessment (hukumat 'adl), not diya. Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal rulings regarding minors (الصبيان) drawn from various authoritative Hanafi sources such as al-Multaqat, al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, al-Umda, al-Kanz, al-Bazzaziyya, and others. The text covers a wide range of fiqh chapters, demonstrating that a minor's legal capacity is nuanced: in some areas (like owning property by seizure, accepting gifts, slaughter with conditions) the minor is treated similarly to an adult, while in others (like divorce, manumission, oaths, litigation) their actions are either invalid or contingent upon guardianship. Key principles include: (1) the discerning minor (المميز) has limited capacity in transactions; (2) the minor's intention (niyyah) is considered in matters like zakat where the principal's intention is paramount; (3) the minor's criminal liability is limited – their 'aqila pays diya for unintended killings, but they are not subject to qasama or jizya; (4) in worship, the minor's Islam and apostasy are valid, but apostasy does not incur execution; (5) the minor's testimony and oaths are not accepted; (6) contracts that are purely harmful are void, while those with potential benefit require guardian approval. The passage also notes the authority of al-Umadi's collection for further details. Overall, it reflects the Hanafi approach of balancing the minor's evolving capacity with protective guardianship.

Key Terms
المراهق (al-murahiq): An adolescent near puberty, whose sexual desire is considered relevant for rulings like tahlil.
التحليل (al-tahlil): The act of marrying a thrice-divorced woman to make her permissible for her first husband.
التسمية (al-tasmiya): Saying 'Bismillah' before slaughtering.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced

Minor's Liability and Criminal Matters
Rulings on minor's liability for harm, exclusion from certain penalties, and rules for usurpation and causing death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a minor's actions incur liability and apply the rules regarding diya, qasama, usurpation, and government fines.

Core Idea
A minor's actions can incur liability (damages) through his 'aqila, but he is exempt from qasama, jizya, and government fines.

This final portion of the source passage addresses the minor's involvement in liability and criminal law. It covers diverse topics such as the minor's exclusion from qasama (oath-based collective responsibility), the liability of his 'aqila for diya when a body is found in his house, and the rules for usurpation (ghasb) and causing death. The Hanafi approach is to treat the minor as capable of actions that cause harm (hence liability on his 'aqila) but not as a full subject of certain legal procedures (qasama) or taxes (jizya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the harm caused: diya, qasama, usurpation, killing
Determine whether the case involves unintentional killing, found dead body, usurpation, or direct causing of death. Each has a different ruling.
Qasama is a collective oath in cases of suspected homicide.
2
Apply the exclusion rules
The minor does not enter into qasama. If a dead body is found in his house, diya is on his 'aqila, not on him directly. No jizya on him, no government fines. He is not killed in war if he does not fight.
These exclusions protect the minor from severe penalties.
3
Understand liability for actions
The minor is liable for what he destroys (يضمن ما أتلفه) because actions are not restricted. For usurpation, if someone usurps a minor, the usurper is imprisoned until he returns him. If a minor is given a knife and kills another, diya is on minor's 'aqila, who then can claim from the giver. If a minor falls from a tree on orders, the orderer guarantees diya.
Liability often falls on the 'aqila (tribal insurance) or the instigator.
4
Check the minor's age and understanding
Age matters: a nine-year-old is considered capable of self-protection; younger ones may incur kaffara on the guardian. Also, if the minor is tricked into going, the trickster is liable.
The passage includes nuances based on age.

الملتقط
ويصح توكيله إذا كان يعقد العقد ويقصده ولو محجورا، ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه في نحو بيع بل لموكله وكذا في دفع الزكاة والاعتبار لنيَّة الموكل، ويعمل بقول المميز في المعاملات كهدية ونحوها وفي الملتقط ولا تصح الخصومة من الصبي إلا أن يكون مأذونا . (اهـ).
·
ويحصل بوطئه التحليل للمطلقة ثلاثا إذا كان مراهقا تتحرك آلته النساء . ويشتهي ويملك المال بالاستيلاء على المُباح كالبالغ، والتقاطه كالتقاط البالغ، ويجب ردّ سلامه، ويصح إسلامه وردته ولا يقتل لو ارتد بعد إسلامه صغيرًا أو تبعًا. وتحلّ ذبيحته بشرط أن يعقل التسمية ويضبطها بأن يعلم أن الحل لا يحصل إلا بها؛ كذا في الكافي. ويؤكل الصيد برميه إذا سمى، وليس كالبالغ في النظر إلى الأجنبية والخلوة بها فيجوز له الدخول على النساء إلى خمس عشرة سنة، كما في الملتقط. ولا يقع طلاقه ولا عتقه إلا حكمًا في مسائل ذكرناها في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الطلاق، والحجر عليه في الأقوال كلها لا في الأفعال فيضمن ما أتلفه إلا في مسائل ذكرناه في النوع الثاني من الفوائد في الحجر، وتثبت حرمة المصاهرة بوطئه إن كان ممن يشتهي النساء وإلا فلا. وتثبت أيضًا بوطء الصبية المشتهاة وهي بنت تسع على المختار، ولا يدخل الصبي في القسامة ،والعاقلة وإن وجد قتيل في داره فالدية على عاقلته كما في الصغرى، ولا جزية عليه ولا يدخل في الغرامات السلطانية كما في قسمة الولوالجية، ولا يؤخذ صبيان أهل الذمة بالتمييز عن صبيان المسلمين كما في الخانية، ولا شيء على صبيان بني تغلب.
ولا يقتل ولد الحربي إذا لم يقاتل، ولو قتله مجاهد بعد قول الإمام من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه لم يستحق السلب إلا إذا قاتل، ويدخل الصبي تحت قوله من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه فإذا قتل الصبي استحق سلب مقتوله لقول الزيلعي: ويدخل فيه كل من يستحق الغنيمة سهما أو رضحًا. (انتهى).
،
وفي الكنز أن الصبي ممن يرضخ له إذا قاتل ولو قال السلطان لصبي إذا أدركت فصل بالناس الجمعة جاز، وفي البزازية السلطان أو الوالي إذا كان غير بالغ
فبلغ يحتاج إلى تقليد جديد. (انتهى).
ولا تنعقد يمينه ولو كان مأذونا فباع فوجد المشتري به عيبا لا يحلفه حتى يدرك كما في العمدة، ولو ادَّعى على صبي محجور ولا بينة له لا يحضره إلى باب القاضي لأنه لو حلف فنكل لا يقضي عليه كذا في العمدة ويُقام التعزير عليه تأديبا، وتتوقف عقوده المترددة بين النفع والضرر على إجازة وليه ويصح قبضه للهبة، ولا
يتوقف من أقواله ما تمحض ضررًا ومنه إقراضه واستقراضه لو كان محجورًا، لا لو كان مأذونا وكفالته باطلة ولو عن أبيه، وصحت له وعنه مطلقا .
وقد جمع العمادي في فصوله أحكام الصبيان فمن أراد الاطلاع على كثرة فروعنا وحُسْن تقريرنا واستيعابنا وعلى نِعَم الله تعالى علينا فيما نقصده من جمع المتفرق فلينظر ما ذكره العمادي، وقد ذكر العمادي ما يكون به بالغا، وما يتعلق به تركناه قصدًا لتصريحهم به في كتاب الحجر، وكتابنا هذا إن شاء الله تعالى كتاب المفردات الملتقطات .
الصبية التي لا تُشتَهَى يجوز السفر بها بغير محرم ولا يضمن الصبي بالغصب فلو غصب صبيا فمات عنده لم يضمنه إلا إذا نقله إلى أرض مسبعة أو مكان الوباء أو الحمى، وقد سُئِلتُ عمَّن أخذ ابن إنسان صغيرًا وأخرجه من البلد هل يلزمه إحضاره إلى أبيه ؟ فأجبت بما في الخانية :
رجل غصب صبيا حرًا فغاب الصبي عن يده فإن الغاصب يُحبَس حتى يجيء بالصبي أو يعلم أنه مات (انتهى). ولو خدعه حتى أخذه برضاه لم يضمن كما في الخانية، لأنه ما غصبه لأنه الأخذ قهرًا وفي الملتقط من النكاح وعن محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيمن خدع بنت رجل أو امرأته وأخرجها من منزله. قال أحبسه أبدًا حتى يأتي بها أو يعلم موتها. (انتهى). ولو قطع طرف صبي لم تعلم صحته ففيه حكومة عدل لا دية ولو دفع السكين إلى صبي فقتل نفسه لم يضمن الدافع، وإن قتل غيره فالدية على عاقلة الصبي، ويرجعون بها على الدافع. وكذا لو أمر صبيا بقتل إنسان فقتله، ولو أمر صبيا بالوقوع من شجرة فوقع ضمن ديته، ولو أرسله في حاجة فعطب ضمنه وكذا لو أمره بصعود شجرة لنقض ثمارها فوقع، وكذا لو أمره بكسر الحطب كذا في الخانية، وفيها أيضًا : صبي ابن تسع سنين سقط من سطح أو غرق في ماء ؛ قال بعضهم لا شيء على الوالدين لأنه ممن يحفظ نفسه، وإن كان لا يعقل أو كان أصغر سنًا ؛ قالوا يكون على الوالدين أو على من كان الصبي في حجره الكفارة لترك الحفظ، وقال بعضهم ليس على الوالدين شيء إلا الاستغفار وهو الصحيح، إلا أن يسقط من يده فعليه الكفَّارة، ولو حمل صبيا على دابة وقال أمسكها لي وهي واقفة فسقط ومات كان على عاقلة الذي حمله الدية مطلقا، وإن سير الصبي الدابة فوطأت إنسانًا فقتلته فالدّية على عاقلة الصبي، إلا أن يكون الصبي
Al-Multaqat. His agency is valid if he contracts and intends it, even if under guardianship, and rights do not revert to him in transactions like sale, but to his principal; similarly in giving zakat, consideration is to the principal's intention, and the discerning minor's word is accepted in transactions like gifts and similar; in al-Multaqat: litigation from a minor is not valid unless he is authorized. (End). And his intercourse effects tahlil for a thrice-divorced woman if he is an adolescent whose organ is aroused by women and he desires. He owns property by seizing permissible things like an adult, and his finding (luqata) is like that of an adult, and his greeting must be returned. His Islam and apostasy are valid, but he is not killed if he apostatizes after becoming Muslim as a minor or by following. His slaughter is lawful provided he understands the tasmiya and grasps it, knowing that lawfulness is only attained by it; thus in al-Kafi. His game is eaten by his shot if he says the name, and he is not like an adult in looking at a non-mahram woman or seclusion with her; he may enter upon women up to fifteen years, as in al-Multaqat. His divorce and manumission do not take effect except legally in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in divorce; and he is under interdiction in all statements, not in actions, so he guarantees what he destroys, except in cases we mentioned in the second type of benefits in interdiction. The prohibition of affinity is established by his intercourse if he is one who desires women, otherwise not. It is also established by intercourse with a desired girl who is nine years old according to the chosen view. The minor does not enter into qasama, and the 'aqila: if a slain person is found in his house, the diya is on his 'aqila as in al-Sughra. No jizya on him, nor does he enter into government fines as in Qismat al-Walwalijiyya. The children of dhimmis are not distinguished from Muslim children as in al-Khaniyya, and nothing is on the children of Banu Taghlib. The child of a harbi is not killed if he does not fight, and if a fighter kills him after the imam's saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', he does not deserve the spoils unless he fought. The minor enters under the saying 'whoever kills a slain [enemy] gets his spoils', so if a minor kills, he deserves the spoils of his victim due to al-Zayla'i's saying: everyone who deserves a share of booty or a small grant enters it. (End). And in al-Kanz: the minor is one who is given a small grant if he fights. If the sultan says to a minor 'when you reach puberty, lead the people in Friday prayer', it is permissible. In al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan or governor is not an adult and then reaches puberty, he needs a new appointment. (End). His oath is not valid, even if authorized; if he sells and the buyer finds a defect, he does not make him swear until he reaches puberty as in al-Umda. If a claim is made against a minor under guardianship and the claimant has no evidence, he is not brought to the judge's door because if he were to swear and then refuse, no judgment would be passed against him, thus in al-Umda. Ta'zir is established upon him as discipline. His contracts that are ambiguous between benefit and harm are contingent on his guardian's permission. His acceptance of a gift is valid. And among his statements that are purely harmful are not subject to [contingency], including his lending and borrowing if he is under guardianship, not if authorized. His suretyship is void even if for his father, but valid for him and from him absolutely. Al-Umadi has collected the rulings of minors in his chapters; whoever wishes to see the abundance of our branches, the goodness of our presentation, and our comprehensiveness, and the blessings of Allah upon us in our aim of gathering scattered [rulings], let him look at what al-Umadi mentioned. And al-Umadi has mentioned what makes one an adult, and what relates to that we have omitted intentionally because they have stated it in the book of interdiction, and this book of ours, Allah willing, is the book of unique collected items. A girl who is not desired: it is permissible to travel with her without a mahram. A minor does not guarantee by usurpation; if someone usurps a minor and he dies in his possession, he does not guarantee him unless he moved him to a land full of beasts or a place of plague or fever. I was asked about one who took a small son of a person and took him out of the town: is he required to bring him back to his father? I answered with what is in al-Khaniyya: A man usurped a free minor and the minor disappeared from his hand; then the usurper is imprisoned until he brings the minor or learns that he died. (End). If he tricked him until he took him with his consent, he does not guarantee, as in al-Khaniyya, because he did not usurp him since usurpation is taking by force. In al-Multaqat from Nikah: from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, concerning one who tricked a man's daughter or his wife and took her out of his house. He said: I would imprison him forever until he brings her or knows her death. (End). If someone cuts a limb of a minor whose health is unknown, there is an equitable assessment (hukumat 'adl), not diya. If someone hands a knife to a minor and he kills himself, the giver does not guarantee; if he kills another, the diya is on the minor's 'aqila, and they claim it back from the giver. Similarly, if he orders a minor to kill a man and he kills him. If he orders a minor to fall from a tree and he falls, he guarantees his diya. If he sends him on an errand and he perishes, he guarantees him; similarly, if he orders him to climb a tree to pick its fruits and he falls, and similarly if he orders him to break firewood, thus in al-Khaniyya. In it also: a minor of nine years fell from a roof or drowned in water; some say nothing is on the parents because he is one who can protect himself; if he was not intelligent or younger, they said there is kaffara on the parents or on the one in whose care the minor was for neglecting protection; and some said nothing is on the parents except seeking forgiveness, and that is the correct view, unless he fell from his hand, then kaffara is upon him. If he placed a minor on an animal and said 'hold it for me' while it was standing, and the minor fell and died, the diya is on the 'aqila of the one who placed him absolutely. If the minor made the animal walk and it trampled a man and killed him, the diya is on the minor's 'aqila, unless the minor...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of legal rulings regarding minors (الصبيان) drawn from various authoritative Hanafi sources such as al-Multaqat, al-Kafi, al-Khaniyya, al-Umda, al-Kanz, al-Bazzaziyya, and others. The text covers a wide range of fiqh chapters, demonstrating that a minor's legal capacity is nuanced: in some areas (like owning property by seizure, accepting gifts, slaughter with conditions) the minor is treated similarly to an adult, while in others (like divorce, manumission, oaths, litigation) their actions are either invalid or contingent upon guardianship. Key principles include: (1) the discerning minor (المميز) has limited capacity in transactions; (2) the minor's intention (niyyah) is considered in matters like zakat where the principal's intention is paramount; (3) the minor's criminal liability is limited – their 'aqila pays diya for unintended killings, but they are not subject to qasama or jizya; (4) in worship, the minor's Islam and apostasy are valid, but apostasy does not incur execution; (5) the minor's testimony and oaths are not accepted; (6) contracts that are purely harmful are void, while those with potential benefit require guardian approval. The passage also notes the authority of al-Umadi's collection for further details. Overall, it reflects the Hanafi approach of balancing the minor's evolving capacity with protective guardianship.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasama): A collective oath taken by the community in cases of suspected homicide when there is evidence.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The paternal relatives who are liable for paying diya in cases of unintentional killing.
الغصب (al-ghasb): Unlawful usurpation of someone else's property or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a minor kills an enemy soldier in battle?
A) He does not deserve any spoils because he is a minor.
B) He deserves the spoils because he is included in the rule.
C) The spoils go to his guardian.
D) He cannot participate in battle.

Key Takeaway
A minor's actions can incur liability (diya on 'aqila), but he is exempt from qasama, jizya, and government fines.

The Legal Definition of Drunkenness and Its Application
Defines drunkenness with ikhtilaf and its implications for wudu and oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi definitions of drunkenness, apply the mufta bihi definition to cases of wudu nullification and oaths, and explain the rule regarding qada of prayers from permissible intoxication.

Core Idea
The drunkard is defined by confused speech (Sahibayn's view) — this governs wudu and oath rulings.

This passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on the definition of drunkenness. While the Great Imam Abu Hanifa defined it as complete disorientation, his two students set a lower threshold of confused speech. The passage explains which view is relied upon for fatwa in matters of purification and oaths, and also addresses a subtle point about intoxication from permissible sources. Understanding this distinction is crucial for issuing correct fatwas in cases involving intoxication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
Locate the two definitions of sukran in the text. Note which imam held each definition.
Abu Hanifa: one who cannot distinguish earth/sky or man/woman. Sahibayn: one with confused speech and delirium.
2
Understand the scope of tarjih
The text states that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view for nullification of wudu and oaths. Recognize that this tarjih is based on precaution (ihtiyat) in prohibitions.
The phrase 'المعتبر في القدح المسكر في حق الحرمة ما قالاه احتياطا في المحرمات' indicates this caution.
3
Analyze the tanbih
Read the note about intoxication from a permissible source (like unripe dates). Understand the exception: it is like unconsciousness but missed prayers must still be made up because the person caused it by his own action.
Key difference: qada is not waived even if the duration exceeds a day and night.
4
Apply the definition
Given a scenario, determine if a person is legally drunk per the mufta bihi definition and what legal effects follow for wudu and oaths.
Use the Sahibayn's criterion: check for confusion in speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في حدّ السكران فقيل : مَن لا يعرف الأرض من السماء والرجل من المرأة. وبه قال الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله . وقيل : مَن في كلامه اختلاط وهذيان، وهو قولهما وبه أخذ كثير من المشايخ والمعتبر في القدح المُسكِر في حق الحرمة ما قالاه احتياطا في المحرَّمات والخلاف في الحدّ والفتوى على قولهما في انتقاض الطهارة به وفي يمينه ألا يُسكر كما بيناه في شرح الكنز.
تنبيه :
قولهم إن السكر من مُباح كالإغماء، يُستثنى منه سقوط القضاء فإنه لا يسقط عنه وإن كان أكثر من يوم وليلة لأنه بصنعه ؛ كذا في المحيط .
And there is disagreement concerning the definition of the drunkard. It was said: one who does not distinguish the earth from the sky nor a man from a woman. And this was the view of the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa), may Allah have mercy on him. And it was said: one in whose speech there is confusion and delirium, and this is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and many of the mashayikh adopted it. And the considered view regarding the intoxicating cup in terms of prohibition is what they (the two) said, out of precaution in prohibitions. The disagreement is in the definition, and the fatwa is on their view regarding the nullification of wudu by it, and regarding his oath not to become intoxicated, as we explained in Sharh al-Kanz.
A note:
Their statement that intoxication from a permissible source is like unconsciousness is excepted from it the lapse of missed prayers, for it (the prayer) does not lapse from him even if it is more than a day and a night, because it is due to his own action. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal definition of a drunkard (sukran) and its consequences. It begins by presenting the ikhtilaf (disagreement) between Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifa defined a drunkard as one who cannot distinguish the earth from the sky or a man from a woman – a very high threshold. The two students defined it more broadly: one whose speech is confused and delirious. The text notes that many later scholars adopted the students' view, and it is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) for matters of tahara (wudu) and oaths. The author then adds a note (tanbih): if intoxication occurs from a permissible source (like eating unripe dates without intent to become drunk), it is like unconsciousness in that it does not nullify prayers, but unlike unconsciousness, missed prayers must still be made up because the person caused it by his own action.

Key Terms
السكران (al-sukran): legally defined person who has lost intellect due to intoxication; debated between two definitions
الحد (al-hadd): the legal definition or criterion
الخلاف (al-khilaf): disagreement among Hanafi imams

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa position in this text, which definition of drunkenness is used to determine nullification of wudu?
A) One who cannot distinguish earth from sky
B) One who cannot distinguish a man from a woman
C) One whose speech is confused and delirious
D) One who vomits after drinking

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers two definitions of drunkenness; for fatwa on wudu and oaths, the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view requiring confused speech.

Family and Personal Status Rulings for Slaves
Extracting family and personal status rulings from a comprehensive list.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a female slave's maintenance, the requirement of istibra', and the consequences of a master's claim of paternity.

Core Idea
A female slave's maintenance requires housing; her child is not affiliated without master's claim; intercourse needs istibra'.

This lesson extracts key rulings from a comprehensive passage on the legal status of slaves in Hanafi Fiqh, focusing on family and personal status matters. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for muftis when issuing fatwas regarding slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on dower and child lineage.
Read the first sentence: 'و مهرها كغيرها ولا يلحق ولدها مولاها إلا بدعوته منه ولو أقرَّ بوطئها'. State that dower is like free woman's, but child affiliation requires the master's claim.
Even if master admits intercourse, child not automatically his.
2
Determine the period of Ila' and the condition for maintenance.
Next: 'وإيلاء الأمة المنكوحة شهران ولا خادم لها ولو جميلة ولا تجب نفقتها إلا بالتبوئة'. Ila' period is two months; no servant is provided; maintenance only with housing (tabwi'a).
Tabwi'a means providing a dwelling.
3
Apply the rule of istibra' and others.
Then: 'ولا توطأ إلا بعد الاستبراء بخلاف الحرّة، ولا حصر لعدد السراري، ويجوز جمعهنَّ في مسكن واحد بدون الرضاء'. Intercourse only after istibra'; no limit on concubines; can house them together without consent.
Istibra' is one menstrual cycle.
4
Identify prohibitions and custody.
Next: 'ولا ظهار ولا إيلاء من أمته، ولا مطالبة لها إذا كان مولاها عنينا، ولا حضانة لأقاربه بل لسيده'. Zihar and Ila' not applicable; slave cannot claim divorce if master impotent; custody goes to master.
This differs from free woman's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و مهرها كغيرها ولا يلحق ولدها مولاها إلا بدعوته منه ولو أقرَّ بوطئها، وإيلاء الأمة المنكوحة شهران ولا خادم لها ولو جميلة ولا تجب نفقتها إلا بالتبوئة(۱) ولا توطأ إلا بعد الاستبراء بخلاف الحرّة، ولا حصر لعدد السراري، ويجوز جمعهنَّ في مسكن واحد بدون الرضاء، ولا ظهار ولا إيلاء من أمته، ولا مطالبة لها إذا كان مولاها عنينا، ولا حضانة لأقاربه بل لسيده ولا قصاص بينه وبين الحر في الأطراف. بخلاف النفس، وتجب الحكومة بحلق لحيته ودواؤه مريضًا على مولاه، بخلاف الحر ولو زوجة، وإذا لم يقدر على الوضوء إلا بمعين فعلى السيد أن يرضيه بخلاف الحر، ولا يتزوج إلا بإذن مولاه ومهره متعلق برقبته كالدين ويُباع في نفقة زوجته، ولا تجب عليه نفقة ولده ولا نفقة لها إلا بالتبوئة ولا تسمع الدعوى والشهادة عليه إلا بحضور سيده ولا يحبس في دين، ويملكه الكفار بالاستيلاء، ولا يصح تصادق العبد والأمة على النكاح إلا المسبيين قبل القسمة بخلاف الحرين كما في التاتارخانية، وإعتاقه باطل ولو معلقا بما يملكه بعد عتقه وكذا وصيته وهبته وصدقته وتبرعه إلا إهداء اليسير من المأذون والمُحابات اليسيرة منه والإذن في العزل إلى مولاها وهو المطالب لزوجها العنين والمجبوب بالتفريق وليس مصرفًا للصدقات الواجبة إلا إذا كان مولاه فقيرًا أو كان مكاتبا، ولا يتحمل عنه مولاه مؤنة إلا دم إحصاره عن إحرام مأذون فيه ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه لو وكيلاً محجورا، ولا جزية عليه، ولا يدخل في القسامة، ووطء إحدى الأمتين ليس بيانًا للعتق المبهم، بخلاف وطء إحدى المرأتين لا يكون بيانًا في الطلاق المبهم وأمره عبده بإتلاف شيء موجب لضمانه وأمر عبد الغير بإتلاف مال غير مولاه موجب للضمان على الآمر مطلقا بخلاف الحرّ إلا إذا كان سلطانًا ويضمن بالغصب بخلاف الحر ولو صغيرا، ولا يصح وقفه، وعقده موقوف على إجازة مولاه .
(۱) التبوئة : التمكن منها .
And her dower is like that of a free woman. Her child is not affiliated to her master except by his claim, even if he acknowledged intercourse. The period of Ila' for a married female slave is two months. She has no servant even if she is beautiful. Maintenance is not obligatory for her except with housing (tabwi'a). She is not to be intercourse with except after istibra', unlike a free woman. There is no limit to the number of concubines, and it is permissible to collect them in one dwelling without their consent. There is no Zihar or Ila' from one's female slave. She has no claim if her master is impotent. Custody for his relatives is not allowed, rather for her master. There is no qisas between him and a free person in limbs, unlike life. Government (compensation) is due for shaving his beard and treating his illness on his master, unlike a free person, even if a wife. If he cannot perform wudu without assistance, the master must provide it, unlike a free person. He may not marry without his master's permission, and his dower is attached to his person like a debt. He is sold for his wife's maintenance. Maintenance for his child is not obligatory on him, nor maintenance for her except with housing. Lawsuit and testimony are not heard against him except in the presence of his master, and he is not imprisoned for debt. Disbelievers own him by capture. The mutual acknowledgment of marriage by a male slave and female slave is not valid except for captives before division, unlike two free persons, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. His emancipation is void, even if suspended on something he will own after his emancipation, and likewise his will, gift, charity, and donation, except a small gift from an authorized slave and small favors from him, and permission to isolate his sperm to his master. He is the one who demands separation from her impotent husband or a eunuch. He is not a recipient of obligatory charity unless his master is poor or he is a mukatib. His master does not bear expenses for him except the blood of ihsar for a permitted ihram. Rights are not returned to him if he is a restricted agent. There is no jizya on him and he does not enter into the qasama. Intercourse with one of two female slaves is not a clarification of ambiguous emancipation, unlike intercourse with one of two women which is not a clarification in ambiguous divorce. If he orders his slave to destroy something, it is subject to his guarantee. If he orders someone else's slave to destroy property not belonging to the master, it is subject to guarantee on the orderer absolutely, unlike a free person, unless he is a sultan. He is liable for usurpation, unlike a free person, even if young. His endowment is not valid, and his contract is suspended upon his master's permission.
(1) al-Tabwi'a: providing accommodation.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive list of rulings concerning slaves (male and female) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by establishing that a female slave's dower (mahr) is the same as a free woman's, but her child does not trace lineage to the master unless he claims it. The period of Ila' (vow of abstinence) for a married female slave is two months, half that of a free woman. Maintenance (nafaqa) is only obligatory if the master provides her with a dwelling (tabwi'a). Intercourse with a newly purchased slave is prohibited until after istibra' (one menstrual cycle to ensure no pregnancy from previous owner). There is no limit to the number of concubines a man may own, and they may be housed together without their consent. Zihar (injurious comparison) and Ila' are not applicable from a master to his female slave. If the master is impotent, the slave has no claim for divorce. Custody of her child belongs to the master, not the slave's relatives. Qisas (retaliation) for limbs is not applicable between a slave and a free person, but for life it is. Compensation (government) is due for harming a slave's beard or providing medical treatment at the master's expense. The master must provide assistance for wudu if the slave cannot manage alone. A slave cannot marry without permission, and his dower is a debt on his person. He can be sold to pay his wife's maintenance. Testimony and lawsuits require the master's presence. A slave taken captive by disbelievers becomes their property. Mutual acknowledgment of marriage by slaves is invalid unless they are captives before division. The slave's emancipation is void, even if suspended. His financial transactions (will, gift, charity) are generally invalid except small gifts if he is authorized. The slave is responsible for demanding dissolution of his wife's marriage if the husband is impotent. He cannot receive obligatory charity unless his master is poor or he is a mukatib (contracting for freedom). The master bears expenses only for the blood of ihsar (being prevented from Hajj). He is not subject to jizya or qasama (oath for murder). Intercourse with one of two female slaves does not clarify which was intended for emancipation, unlike analogous cases for divorce. If a master orders his slave to destroy property, the master guarantees it. If a free person orders a slave to destroy another's property, the orderer guarantees it absolutely. The slave is liable for usurpation (ghasb) unlike a free person. His endowment (waqf) is invalid, and his contracts are suspended on the master's permission.

Key Terms
التبوئة (al-tabwi'a): Providing accommodation for the female slave.
الاستبراء (al-istibra'): Waiting period of one menstrual cycle after acquisition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the period of Ila' for a married female slave?
A) Four months
B) Two months
C) One month
D) Six months

Key Takeaway
A female slave's maintenance depends on housing, and her child's lineage requires the master's claim.

Marriage and Financial Transactions of Slaves
Rules for marriage and financial transactions of slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules for a slave's marriage, financial transactions, and the validity of contracts such as emancipation and wills.

Core Idea
A slave cannot marry without master's permission; his dower is a debt on his person; his emancipation and donations are void unless authorized.

This lesson covers the legal capacity of slaves in matters of marriage and financial dealings. These rules ensure that the master's rights are protected while allowing limited autonomy for the slave where permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the marriage permission rule.
Read: 'ولا يتزوج إلا بإذن مولاه ومهره متعلق برقبته كالدين'. A slave cannot marry without master's permission; his dower is attached to his person like a debt.
The dower becomes a debt owed by the slave, not the master.
2
Examine the consequences of marriage and maintenance.
Then: 'ويُباع في نفقة زوجته، ولا تجب عليه نفقة ولده ولا نفقة لها إلا بالتبوئة ولا تسمع الدعوى والشهادة عليه إلا بحضور سيده ولا يحبس في دين'. He can be sold to pay his wife's maintenance; he is not obligated for child or wife maintenance (wife only if tabwi'a); lawsuits require master's presence; he is not imprisoned for debt.
This shows limited financial liability.
3
Analyze the rules for emancipation and donations.
Next: 'وإعتاقه باطل ولو معلقا بما يملكه بعد عتقه وكذا وصيته وهبته وصدقته وتبرعه إلا إهداء اليسير من المأذون والمُحابات اليسيرة منه والإذن في العزل إلى مولاها'. A slave's emancipation is void; likewise his will, gift, charity, donation—except small gifts from an authorized slave and small favors, and permission for coitus interruptus.
Only small transactions from an authorized slave are valid.
4
Understand other restrictions.
Remaining: 'وهو المطالب لزوجها العنين والمجبوب بالتفريق وليس مصرفًا للصدقات الواجبة إلا إذا كان مولاه فقيرًا أو كان مكاتبا، ولا يتحمل عنه مولاه مؤنة إلا دم إحصاره عن إحرام مأذون فيه ولا ترجع الحقوق إليه لو وكيلاً محجورا، ولا جزية عليه، ولا يدخل في القسامة'. He demands dissolution for his wife's impotent husband; cannot receive obligatory charity unless master poor or he is mukatib; master bears only blood money for ihsar; no jizya; not in qasama.
The slave has limited roles in legal processes.

Key Terms
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave given permission by his master to engage in trade.
المكاتب (al-mukatib): A slave who has a contract to earn his freedom by paying installments.

Liability and Legal Capacity of Slaves
Rules on liability and capacity of slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rules on qisas, compensation, guarantee, and contractual capacity of slaves, and identify where they differ from free persons.

Core Idea
A slave is not subject to qisas for limbs; his master compensates for his acts; his contracts are suspended.

This lesson examines the liability of slaves in criminal and civil matters, and their capacity to make contracts. The rulings emphasize the master's responsibility while limiting the slave's independent legal actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule on qisas for limbs vs. life.
Read: 'ولا قصاص بينه وبين الحر في الأطراف. بخلاف النفس'. There is no qisas between a slave and free person for limbs, but there is for life.
Qisas for life applies, but limbs are compensated by government (compensation).
2
Examine compensation (government) for harm.
Then: 'وتجب الحكومة بحلق لحيته ودواؤه مريضًا على مولاه، بخلاف الحر ولو زوجة، وإذا لم يقدر على الوضوء إلا بمعين فعلى السيد أن يرضيه بخلاف الحر'. Government (compensation) is due for shaving his beard and medical treatment on the master; wudu assistance must be provided.
The master bears the cost for such harms.
3
Analyze guarantee and destruction of property.
Next: 'وأمره عبده بإتلاف شيء موجب لضمانه وأمر عبد الغير بإتلاف مال غير مولاه موجب للضمان على الآمر مطلقا بخلاف الحرّ إلا إذا كان سلطانًا ويضمن بالغصب بخلاف الحر ولو صغيرا'. If master orders slave to destroy property, master guarantees. If orderer is free, he guarantees absolutely. Slave is liable for ghasb (usurpation) unlike free person.
The slave is treated like a tool in some cases, but personally liable in ghasb.
4
Understand contractual capacity.
Finally: 'ولا يصح وقفه، وعقده موقوف على إجازة مولاه'. His endowment (waqf) is invalid; his contracts are suspended on master's permission.
No independent contractual capacity beyond limited permission.

(۱) التبوئة : التمكن منها .
And her dower is like that of a free woman. Her child is not affiliated to her master except by his claim, even if he acknowledged intercourse. The period of Ila' for a married female slave is two months. She has no servant even if she is beautiful. Maintenance is not obligatory for her except with housing (tabwi'a). She is not to be intercourse with except after istibra', unlike a free woman. There is no limit to the number of concubines, and it is permissible to collect them in one dwelling without their consent. There is no Zihar or Ila' from one's female slave. She has no claim if her master is impotent. Custody for his relatives is not allowed, rather for her master. There is no qisas between him and a free person in limbs, unlike life. Government (compensation) is due for shaving his beard and treating his illness on his master, unlike a free person, even if a wife. If he cannot perform wudu without assistance, the master must provide it, unlike a free person. He may not marry without his master's permission, and his dower is attached to his person like a debt. He is sold for his wife's maintenance. Maintenance for his child is not obligatory on him, nor maintenance for her except with housing. Lawsuit and testimony are not heard against him except in the presence of his master, and he is not imprisoned for debt. Disbelievers own him by capture. The mutual acknowledgment of marriage by a male slave and female slave is not valid except for captives before division, unlike two free persons, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. His emancipation is void, even if suspended on something he will own after his emancipation, and likewise his will, gift, charity, and donation, except a small gift from an authorized slave and small favors from him, and permission to isolate his sperm to his master. He is the one who demands separation from her impotent husband or a eunuch. He is not a recipient of obligatory charity unless his master is poor or he is a mukatib. His master does not bear expenses for him except the blood of ihsar for a permitted ihram. Rights are not returned to him if he is a restricted agent. There is no jizya on him and he does not enter into the qasama. Intercourse with one of two female slaves is not a clarification of ambiguous emancipation, unlike intercourse with one of two women which is not a clarification in ambiguous divorce. If he orders his slave to destroy something, it is subject to his guarantee. If he orders someone else's slave to destroy property not belonging to the master, it is subject to guarantee on the orderer absolutely, unlike a free person, unless he is a sultan. He is liable for usurpation, unlike a free person, even if young. His endowment is not valid, and his contract is suspended upon his master's permission.
(1) al-Tabwi'a: providing accommodation.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive list of rulings concerning slaves (male and female) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by establishing that a female slave's dower (mahr) is the same as a free woman's, but her child does not trace lineage to the master unless he claims it. The period of Ila' (vow of abstinence) for a married female slave is two months, half that of a free woman. Maintenance (nafaqa) is only obligatory if the master provides her with a dwelling (tabwi'a). Intercourse with a newly purchased slave is prohibited until after istibra' (one menstrual cycle to ensure no pregnancy from previous owner). There is no limit to the number of concubines a man may own, and they may be housed together without their consent. Zihar (injurious comparison) and Ila' are not applicable from a master to his female slave. If the master is impotent, the slave has no claim for divorce. Custody of her child belongs to the master, not the slave's relatives. Qisas (retaliation) for limbs is not applicable between a slave and a free person, but for life it is. Compensation (government) is due for harming a slave's beard or providing medical treatment at the master's expense. The master must provide assistance for wudu if the slave cannot manage alone. A slave cannot marry without permission, and his dower is a debt on his person. He can be sold to pay his wife's maintenance. Testimony and lawsuits require the master's presence. A slave taken captive by disbelievers becomes their property. Mutual acknowledgment of marriage by slaves is invalid unless they are captives before division. The slave's emancipation is void, even if suspended. His financial transactions (will, gift, charity) are generally invalid except small gifts if he is authorized. The slave is responsible for demanding dissolution of his wife's marriage if the husband is impotent. He cannot receive obligatory charity unless his master is poor or he is a mukatib (contracting for freedom). The master bears expenses only for the blood of ihsar (being prevented from Hajj). He is not subject to jizya or qasama (oath for murder). Intercourse with one of two female slaves does not clarify which was intended for emancipation, unlike analogous cases for divorce. If a master orders his slave to destroy property, the master guarantees it. If a free person orders a slave to destroy another's property, the orderer guarantees it absolutely. The slave is liable for usurpation (ghasb) unlike a free person. His endowment (waqf) is invalid, and his contracts are suspended on the master's permission.

Key Terms
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation of property wrongfully.
الحكومة (al-hukuma): Compensation assessed by a judge for injury not covered by fixed diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a free person orders someone else's slave to destroy property that does not belong to the master, who guarantees the damage?
A) The slave's master
B) The free person who gave the order
C) The slave himself
D) No one

Key Takeaway
A slave's liability is limited; the master bears many responsibilities, and the slave cannot independently enter contracts.

Rulings on the Female Slave and Slave Property in Hanafi Law
Collection of distinct slave rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific Hanafi rulings on a female slave's 'iddah, travel, and property, and apply the principle that a slave's acquisitions belong to the master.

Core Idea
Female slave travels without mahram; her 'iddah shorter; her master owns her acquisitions.

This passage from Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents a series of distinct rulings concerning slaves, particularly the female slave. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi school's detailed treatment of slavery, balancing the slave's legal disabilities with the master's rights. The passage also highlights internal school differences and the importance of correctly identifying the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on 'Iddah and Travel
Read the first sentence: 'في العدة ويحلّ سفرها بغير محرم'. This states that the female slave observes 'iddah and her travel is permissible without a mahram. Note the difference from a free woman.
The specific duration of 'iddah is not given here, but it is known from other sources: two menstrual cycles or 45 days.
2
Identify the ruling on a Slave's Rights
The next part: 'ولا حق له في بيت المال ولا يؤخذ بالتمييز عندنا لو كان عبد ذمي'. This means a slave has no claim to the public treasury, and a dhimmi slave is not subject to tamyiz (discrimination).
Tamyiz likely refers to a specific legal process.
3
Identify the ruling on Waqf on One's Own Slave
Then: 'ولا يصح الوقف على عبد نفسه أو أمته عند محمد رحمه الله إلا المدبر وأم الولد'. According to Imam Muhammad, a waqf on one's own slave is invalid, except for a mudabbar and umm walad.
This shows an intra-Hanafi difference, as the text attributes this view to Muhammad.
4
Identify the ruling on Foundling and Mubah Property
The author notes: 'ولم أر حكم التقاطه أو استيلائه على المباح' – he has not seen a ruling on a slave picking up a foundling or seizing mubah. He opines that in the latter case, the master acquires it.
This is the author's own inference, indicating gaps in the transmitted texts.
5
Identify the ruling on a Returned Runaway Slave
Finally: 'لو ردَّ ابقا فالجعل لمولاه ويعزره مولاه على الصحيح ولا يحدّه'. The reward for returning a runaway goes to the master; the master disciplines but does not impose hadd.
This clarifies the master's disciplinary authority and the limits of corporal punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمة وتخرج
·
في العدة ويحلّ سفرها بغير محرم، ولا حق له في بيت المال ولا يؤخذ بالتمييز عندنا لو كان عبد ذمي.
ولا يصح الوقف على عبد نفسه أو أمته عند محمد رحمه الله إلا المدبر وأم الولد . ولم أر حكم التقاطه أو استيلائه على المباح وينبغي في الثاني أن يملكه مولاه أخدا عندنا .
من قولهم لو ردَّ ابقا فالجعل لمولاه ويعزره مولاه على الصحيح ولا يحدّه
·
ومن نعم الله على عبده تيسير جمعها من محالها ولم أرها مجموعة ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم. اللهم افتح لنا من رحمتك وألهمنا رشدنا .
The female slave and she goes out... in the waiting period (iddah) and her travel is permissible without a mahram. And he has no right in the treasury (bayt al-mal). And he is not taken by discrimination (tamyiz) according to us if he is a dhimmi slave. The endowment (waqf) on one's own slave or female slave is not valid according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) except for a mudabbar and umm walad. I have not seen the ruling on his picking up a foundling or his seizure of permissible (mubah) things. And it is appropriate in the second that his master owns it as an acquisition according to us. From their statement: 'If a runaway slave is returned, the reward (ju'l) goes to his master, and his master disciplines him (yu'azzir) on the correct view, and does not impose hadd punishment.' Then from the blessings of Allah upon His servant is the facilitation of collecting them from their sources, and I have not seen them collected. There is no power or strength except by Allah, the High, the Magnificent. O Allah, open for us from Your mercy and inspire us with our guidance.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on slaves, focusing on the female slave (al-amah) and some additional points. It begins by stating that the female slave performs her 'iddah (waiting period after separation) and that she may travel without a mahram (male guardian), which differs from a free woman. A slave has no right to the state treasury (bayt al-mal). A dhimmi slave is not to be taken by discrimination (tamyiz) – a reference to a specific rule about distinguishing status. Regarding waqf, according to Imam Muhammad, one cannot endow property to one's own slave or female slave, except for a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom after master's death) and umm walad (a female slave who bore a child to her master). The author notes he has not seen a ruling on a slave picking up a foundling (laqit) or seizing ownerless property (mubah); he opines that in the latter case, the master should acquire ownership as a capture (akhdh). If a runaway slave is returned, the reward (ju'l) belongs to the master, and the master may discipline him but not impose a hadd punishment. The passage ends with a personal reflection on the difficulty of collecting these rulings and a supplication.

Key Terms
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period a female slave must observe after separation from her master or after her master's death.
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, granting her certain protections.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, who receives the reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave?
A) The person who found him.
B) The slave himself.
C) The slave's master.
D) The state treasury.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives a female slave greater mobility (travel without mahram) and treats her master as the owner of her acquisitions.

Rulings on the Blind Person
Listing specific rulings for the blind person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general principle for a blind person and list the specific exceptions in obligations, roles, blood money, and other acts, and apply them to determine the Hanafi ruling in a given scenario.

Core Idea
A blind person is like a sighted person except where his lack of sight prevents the act or its reliability.

This passage is a rasm al-mufti listing that compiles the key rulings specific to a blind person across various chapters of fiqh. It serves as a quick reference for muftis, establishing that the blind person is treated like the sighted unless sight is essential for the act or its validity. Understanding these exceptions prevents incorrect imposition of obligations or acceptance of invalid acts.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
The text opens with 'هو كالبصير إلا في مسائل' meaning the blind person is like the sighted except in specific matters. This establishes the baseline: all rulings of a sighted apply unless an exception is listed.
2
List the obligations that are not required
Identify the four obligations that are waived: jihad (جهاد), Friday prayer (جمعة), congregation (جماعة), and Hajj (حج) – even if a guide is available. Sight is necessary for these acts.
These are fard 'ayn that require sight for fulfillment.
3
Identify the positions he cannot hold
The blind person is not qualified for testimony (شهادة) absolutely, nor for judgeship (قضاء), nor for the supreme imamate (إمامة عظمى). These roles require reliability that sight provides.
The relied-upon view (المعتمد) rejects testimony absolutely.
4
Recall the blood money rule
There is no fixed diya for his eye; instead, the compensation is a government valuation (حكومة). This is because the eye of a blind person has no fixed value but some value remains.
5
Note the ruling on leading prayer
It is disliked (يكره) for a blind person to lead prayer unless he is the most knowledgeable of the people. Knowledge overcomes the dislike.
6
Review other acts: manumission, slaughter, custody, etc.
His manumission for expiation is invalid. Slaughter by him is disliked. Custody is conditional on his ability to protect the ward. He is fit to be an overseer (ناظر) or executor (وصي).
The author notes he did not see a ruling on some matters, but gives guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو كالبصير إلا في مسائل :
أحكام الأعمى
منها لا جهاد عليه ولا جمعة ولا جماعة ولا حج وإن وجد قائدا، ولا يصلح للشهادة مطلقا على المعتمد والقضاء والإمامة العظمى، ولا دية في عينه. وإنما الواجب الحكومة، وتكره إمامته إلا أن يكون أعلم القوم، ولا يصح عتقه عن كفَّارة، ولم أرَ حكم ذبحه وصيده وحضانته ورؤيته لما اشتراه بالوصف، وينبغي أن يكره ذبحه وأما حضانته فإن أمكنه حفظ المحضون كان أهلاً وإلا فلا، ويصلح ناظرا أو وصيَّا، والثانية في منظومة ابن وهبان والأولى في أوقاف هلال كما في الإسعاف .
He is like the sighted except in matters: Rulings of the blind. Among them: no jihad upon him, nor Friday prayer, nor congregation, nor Hajj even if he finds a leader; he is not qualified for testimony absolutely according to the relied-upon view, nor for judgeship, nor for the supreme imamate; there is no blood money for his eye, rather the required compensation is the government valuation. It is disliked for him to lead prayer unless he is the most knowledgeable of the people; his manumission is not valid for expiation; I have not seen a ruling on his slaughter, his hunting, his custody, and his sight of what he purchased by description; it is appropriate that his slaughter be disliked; as for his custody, if he can protect the ward, he is qualified, otherwise not; he is fit to be an overseer or executor; the second (view) is in the versification of Ibn Wahban and the first in the endowments of Hilal as in al-Is'af.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage presents a collection of rulings specific to a blind person in various areas of fiqh. The general principle is that a blind person is treated like a sighted person except where incapacity necessitates a different ruling. The text lists specific exceptions: jihad, Friday prayer, congregation, and Hajj are not obligatory even if a guide is available; testimony, judgeship, and supreme imamate are not valid; there is no fixed blood money for his eye but rather a compensation assessed by government experts; leading prayer is disliked unless he is the most knowledgeable; manumission for expiation is invalid; slaughter by him is disliked; custody is conditional on his ability to protect; he may serve as an overseer or executor. The source cites the second view from Ibn Wahban's poem and the first from Hilal's endowments as recorded in al-Is'af. This is a practical list for muftis to apply.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a'mā): A person who is blind, subject to special rulings due to lack of sight.
الحكومة (al-ḥukūma): A compensatory payment determined by valuation, not a fixed amount.
المعتمد (al-muʿtamad): The relied-upon view in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is valid if he has a guide.
B) It is valid in some cases.
C) It is absolutely invalid according to the relied-upon view.
D) It is valid only in financial matters.

Key Takeaway
A blind person retains most rulings of the sighted, but certain obligations and roles are waived or modified due to his inability to see.
